Local News

City Chamber of Commerce Cables Request to Prepare for Revision of Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement 114

▲ Request to Allow the Cotton Textile Industry to Dispatch Representatives

▲ Discussing Increasing Import Taxes on Cotton Fabrics

The City Chamber of Commerce yesterday cabled the National Government, addressed to the Nanjing Executive Yuan, Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and Ministry of Finance: "On the 17th of this month, a letter was received from the Shanghai Silk Mercerized Cotton Textile Trade Association, stating that our Association previously submitted a document to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance on August 3rd, requesting an increase in import taxes on cotton fabrics to protect domestic goods. We believe that the underdevelopment of our national industries is due to many reasons, but the crux of the problem lies in the lack of tariff autonomy. All major powers in the world use tariff barriers to protect their domestic industries, a fact that your ministries are well aware of. Since the late Qing Dynasty, due to the failure of diplomacy, customs taxation has been controlled by foreigners due to unequal treaties. As a result, machine production has advanced rapidly, and the golden age has passed in vain. The national production still remains in the handicraft stage. Even those with aspirations to revitalize industry, although creating new industries, are quickly overwhelmed by foreign goods. This is truly the sub-colonial status described by Sun Yat-sen. Since the establishment of our National Government, we have been deeply aware of this problem and have paid much attention to tariff autonomy. However, those in charge at the time, ignorant of commercial affairs, sought quick solutions, and subsequent scrutiny revealed a lack of practical understanding. Taking the cotton fabrics produced by the members of our association as an example, they have always been a major import, and their impact on the national livelihood is significant. However, the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement signed on May 6, 1920, included them in the category of mutual benefit. When the news spread, the whole country was in an uproar, and a major mistake was made that could not be undone, which we have painfully endured to this day. As the agreement is about to expire, it is appropriate to plan ahead. Our association urgently appeals to you to resolutely announce a tax increase when the agreement expires in 1933, in order to protect domestic goods. We also request that during the preparatory period, our association be allowed to send representatives to contribute their opinions, which would benefit both the national economy and the people's livelihood. Our association has a deeper understanding of the industry and believes that the survival of domestic goods and industries depends on this. We believe that all of you share the same feeling. However, a long time has passed without a response from your ministries, presumably because our association is small and our words are not enough to attract the attention of your ministries. We have learned that the agreement expires on May 6, 1933, which is fast approaching. We urge you to strongly present this matter to the Executive Yuan, Ministry of Finance, etc., for prompt preparation and a clear response to satisfy our expectations." The Association stated that the Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement was formally signed on May 6, 1920, at which time both parties stated in their notes that the tax rates for items 1, 2, and 3 of Part A of the attached schedule would be maintained for three years. After the expiration of the three-year period, the declared tax rates would naturally be revised. The Trade Association believes that the tax rates on cotton fabrics in the aforementioned agreement only benefit the import of goods from the other country. They request that the import tax on cotton fabrics be increased after the expiration of the three-year agreement and that the Trade Association be allowed to send representatives to contribute their opinions during the preparatory period before the expiration of the agreement, which is indeed for the purpose of protecting our country's cotton fabrics. It is appropriate to report the situation and request your approval from the Yuan and Ministries, and to revise the agreement in a timely manner to protect domestic products. We eagerly await your response. The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce respectfully requests. Xiao"

Press Visited the Construction of the City Center Area Yesterday 115

▲ City Government Sends Staff to Host

The Shanghai City Center Municipal Government Building is scheduled to be completed by the end of June next year, and the Municipal Government and various bureaus are scheduled to move into the building to work on July 1st next year. Yesterday afternoon at 1:30 PM, the Municipal Government specially prepared cars to invite more than 50 members of the local press to visit. Tan Wenqing, Section Chief of the First Division of the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, Xue Cixin, Section Chief of the Third Division, Mo Heng, Section Chief of the Fourth Division, Chen Kecheng of the Municipal Government Propaganda Section, Chen Xunyu, and others warmly hosted the visit. The details of the various new constructions in the city center area are recorded as follows:

▲ Design Process: In July 1927, when the Shanghai Municipal Government was established, it first requested the Central Government to determine the scope of the city area, including Wusong, Jiangwan, and other areas. In November 1927, a design committee was established to study various issues related to municipal administration. At the same time, given that the Municipal Government was located in a remote area of West Shanghai and various bureaus were scattered throughout the city, making it inconvenient to conduct business, the idea of constructing a Municipal Government building arose. In September 1928, a committee for the construction of the Municipal Government building was established to prepare everything. In July 1929, the plan for the city center area was announced and a construction committee for the city center area was established to oversee everything. All matters related to the construction of the new Municipal Government building were also assigned to this committee. Although there was a slight suspension due to the war this year, work was resumed as soon as the situation stabilized. After several months of progress, considerable results have been achieved. A summary is provided below:

▲ General Area: The Shanghai Municipal Government believes that the city's population is increasing daily, land prices are rising, and the housing problem is the most difficult to solve. Traffic tools are improving daily, and the width of Shanghai's existing roads is insufficient. Most of the wharves have no connection with the railways, and the concessions extend across the center of the city, while the cross-border construction of roads is expanding daily in the northwest and southwest directions, hindering the development of the city. Therefore, there is a proposal to construct a city center area, defining an area of more than 6,000 acres north of Xiangyin Road, south of Zhayin Road, east of Songhu Road, and west of Zhou Nan Shi Wu Yi. This area is equidistant from Nanjing Road and the Bund to Fanwangdu Road, making transportation convenient. Moreover, the terrain is flat, the air is fresh, and land prices are low. There is also a good plan to lay the foundation for future progress, and the future development is unlimited.

▲ General Description of the New Building: Although the city center area has been designated, it is still an open space, and it is feared that investors will hesitate. Therefore, it was decided to first construct the Municipal Government building in the city center area to show encouragement. In January 1930, a reward was offered for the design of the Municipal Government building. In July of the same year, an architect's office was established to draw formal drawings, and architect Dong Dayou was hired to oversee the project. In May 1931, bidding began, and the Zhusenji construction company won the bid with a price of 548,000 yuan and began construction. Since the groundbreaking ceremony on July 7th, work has been carried out actively. It has now been built to the roof and is engaged in interior decoration. It was originally scheduled to be completed this month, but due to the impact of the war, it must be postponed until May of next year. The new building is 30 meters high, 90 meters long, and 25 meters wide. The exterior adopts the Chinese architectural style, while the interior uses steel and concrete construction. The building has four floors. The ground floor is for offices and a cafeteria, etc. The second floor is for the auditorium (the auditorium is 25 meters wide and 18 meters deep and can accommodate more than 1,200 seats), conference rooms, libraries, etc. The third floor is for offices, and the fourth floor is for archives and storage rooms, etc.

▲ Bureau Buildings: As the new Municipal Government building is about to be completed, but the new bureau buildings have not yet been built, it is planned to temporarily construct temporary office buildings for the various bureaus in the new Municipal Government building that is under construction, so that the Municipal Government and various bureaus can move in at the same time. It is estimated that after the completion of the new Municipal Government building, in addition to the Secretariat, the Finance and Public Works Bureaus can be temporarily attached to it. The remaining bureaus are planned to build two temporary buildings. The Social, Education, and Health Bureaus will be in one building, and the Public Works and Land Bureaus will be in another building. The two buildings are in the shape of a right angle and are located behind the new Municipal Government building, one on the east and one on the west, in the same style and symmetrical to each other. Each building is 96 meters long on the outside, 61 meters long on the inside, and 42 meters wide, and is a three-story new-style building. It is estimated that each building will cost more than 100,000 yuan, and bidding will begin soon to rush the construction so that it can be completed at the same time as the new Municipal Government building.

▲ Police Station Building: The aforementioned temporary office buildings for the various bureaus do not include the Public Security Bureau. The bureau plans to temporarily remain in the South City and first build several police district stations in the city center area, depending on future needs. The one currently being built is one of the stations, and its location is at the corner of Songhu Road and Xiangyin Road, which is the most important location, occupying an area of 3,900 square meters. It is a steel and concrete building with complete equipment and can accommodate more than 100 police officers. The cost, including water and electricity equipment, is estimated to be about 30,000 yuan. Construction began in August of this year and is currently ongoing.

▲ Project Management: The city of Shanghai has a vast area, and all road projects have management offices in suitable locations in each district to facilitate nearby construction. The roads in the city center area officially started construction in December of last year. After the war, work was resumed even more actively. Therefore, the construction of the management office building cannot be delayed. Bidding began at the beginning of this year, but construction was suspended due to the war until July, when work resumed. Its location is on the north bank of the Qiujiang River, surrounded by bamboo fences. Inside the fence, the south is the factory shed, which is where tools are placed. The north has a row of garages, which is where trucks transporting materials are parked. The central square can be used to pile up the applied materials (there is another material factory). At the west end, there are three large open halls for offices. Other affiliated buildings include staff dormitories and long-term worker dormitories. The total cost is 16,000 yuan and was completed in September.

▲ First Public Cemetery: The Municipal Government believes that the city's cemeteries are all privately run, and their benefits are not widely available to the general public. Therefore, the first municipal cemetery was opened in the Gaoyemiao area, and affiliated buildings such as auditoriums were built, covering an area of more than 90,000 square meters. Construction began in June of last year. First, a small river was dug, and the excavated soil was used to fill the ground. A wall was built in front, and there were seven rooms on the left and right of the gatehouse, including the gatekeeper and reception rooms. The two wings are used as temporary mortuaries for keeping coffins before burial. In the center of the garden, facing the gate, is the auditorium, which is a five-room hall in the Chinese palace style and was completed last month. In addition, the cemetery is planned with routes, drains, and roads. This project is currently underway. The cemetery is divided into several areas and is expected to accommodate more than 4,000 graves. The entire project is expected to cost 90,000 yuan.

▲ Road Paving: In order to prosper the city center area, the Shanghai Municipal Government publicly solicited the remaining part of the land acquired last year, totaling more than 800 acres, at a low price in July of last year. All of the land was claimed on the same day. The subgrade earthwork within the scope of this land will be completed by the end of this month, and most of the road surface base has also started construction. It is estimated that it can be completed by the end of the year. All of the people who have claimed land in this area can now start to build houses, because the roads are all open, and it is very convenient to transport materials. The second solicitation of land and the land claimed by the municipal government staff was held in October of last year. The earthwork project for the roads within the scope of this land is scheduled to start at the end of this month and is expected to be completed by next spring. This earthwork is all taken from dredging the Qiujiang River and the Yuanzhang River. Dredging the river and filling the road serve two purposes. Light railways and railcars are now used to transport and pile up the soil to a considerable location. It is estimated that more than 2,000 workers are used, and the amount of soil that has been filled is about 100,000 cubic meters. The budget for the total road filling is 320,000 cubic meters of soil. The width of the roads in the city center is stipulated to be from 15 meters to 35 meters. There are currently 22 roads under construction, with a total length of about 19 kilometers. The total length of roads in the entire area is about 50 kilometers. All roads are built with asphalt surfaces and planted with trees on both sides, and the grass is laid underneath. It can be seen that a beautiful park residential area will appear in front of us. As for the ditches that should be set up under each road, preparations have long been made, and the production of tile pipes has begun, and steel sheet piles have been ordered from Germany. The large-scale arrangement of ditches will begin next spring.

▲ Bridge Construction: The city center area is located on the banks of the Huangpu River, and the Qiujiang River winds through it from west to east. There are six bridges across the Qiujiang River, all built of steel and concrete, and the exterior is made in the Chinese style. Drawings have been made and bidding will begin soon. Construction will begin simultaneously at the end of this month, which will not only facilitate transportation but also add to the scenery of the Qiujiang River.

▲ Park Development: A park is being developed to the southwest of the new Municipal Government building, and a part of it has already started construction. The park has sports fields and tracks, which are also under construction. Trees have been planted separately. The area is about 400 acres, which is larger than Zhaofeng Park. The Qiujiang River runs through it, and the scenery is natural. Therefore, the magnificence and beauty of the city center area in the future will definitely not be comparable to the concessions. In addition, there are three large parks that will be developed soon, as well as many garden areas. The location of the parks is one in the southwest of the new Municipal Government building, one in the southeast, one in the northeast, and one in the northeast on the banks of the Huangpu River. The garden areas outside this include the Jiangwan and Yinxiang racetracks, the Sijing Bridge ball field, and the area along the edge of the city center area.

The Chinese Business Electric Company's Labor Strike: Party and Government Order Resumption of Work 116

▲ After the General Manager Was Rescued, an Emergency Board Meeting Was Held Yesterday

▲ Fortunately, None of the Injured Are in Life-Threatening Condition

After the workers of the Chinese Business Electric Company went on strike, trams on all routes continued to be suspended yesterday. The Municipal Government and the Municipal Party Department discussed the handling of the matter at a meeting in the morning and issued a joint announcement in the afternoon, ordering the workers to resume work before noon today. If they dare to disobey, the employer is allowed to dismiss them and recruit new workers. All public utilities are guarded by armed police officers to protect them. The company held a temporary emergency board meeting. The injured workers and soldiers are not in serious condition.

▲ Rescue of the General Manager: At 9 PM the night before, Wen Yishan, the captain of the Fourth Squadron of the Police Brigade, and Jin Tian, the district chief of the Second District, repeatedly advised the workers who were gathered in the factory and surrounded General Manager Lu Bohong. The workers finally left the factory and dispersed at about 9 PM. Lu Bohong was then escorted out of the factory and returned to his residence by the police officers. By about 10 PM, the soldiers of the Security Brigade were withdrawn, and traffic on Chezhan Road was restored. The Fourth Squadron of the Police Brigade dispatched two squads to guard the factory to prevent incidents. Armed police officers patrolled near the South Railway Station at night, and security was tight.

▲ Protection of Water and Electricity: After the Municipal Government ordered the Public Security Bureau and the Security Office to send police to protect the city's public utilities to prevent the water and electricity supply from being affected, Wen Hongen, the director of the Public Security Bureau, was ordered to send police officers from the Third and Fourth Squadrons of the Police Brigade, and Yang Hu, the director of the Security Office, was ordered to send soldiers from the Tenth Squadron to jointly guard the Gaochangmiao Waterworks and the Chezhan Road Electric Factory that night. The security at the main switch gates was particularly strict, so the city's water and electricity supply will definitely not be affected.

▲ Yesterday's Situation: Starting at 6 AM yesterday morning, workers from the Chinese Business Electric Company went to the company on Chezhan Road one after another. The police officers on guard tried their best to maintain order. It was not until about 9 AM that the workers who had gathered at the company were dispersed and returned to their homes. Only Lu Zhonglin, the director of the Vehicle Department, and tea servants stayed in the company. The gate was closed, leaving only a small door for entry and exit. Police officers from the Fourth Squadron of the Police Brigade guarded the inside and outside of the factory and questioned those entering the factory very strictly. Trams on all routes were still suspended.

▲ Party and Government Meeting: The Party and Government organs held a meeting at the Municipal Party Department on Ximen Linyin Road yesterday morning at 10 AM to discuss concrete handling measures. Those who attended were Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Municipal Party Department members Wu Kaixian, Tao Baichuan, Secretary-General Jiang Huaisu, Security Office Director Yang Hu, Social Bureau Director Wu Xingya, Third Section Chief Xu Yefu, Second Section Chief of the Public Security Bureau Yan Shuzhai, etc. They decided on handling steps and dispersed at 11:30 AM. According to a report from the Xinsheng News Agency reporter, the measures were: first, the Municipal Government and the Municipal Party Department will issue a joint announcement, ordering the workers to resume work before noon on the 20th. If they fail to do so, the employer will be allowed to dismiss them and recruit new workers. As for the injured, after investigation, the perpetrators will be severely punished according to the law.

▲ Joint Announcement: The Central News Agency reported that yesterday, the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government issued a joint announcement regarding the expansion of the Chinese Business Electric Company's labor strike, ordering the resumption of work this afternoon. The full text of the announcement is recorded below. It is a joint announcement regarding the labor-capital dispute of the Chinese Business Electric Company. Since the company's workers submitted a request for a salary increase, the association reviewed it in accordance with the law and sent it to the Social Bureau on October 27th. On November 1st, the Social Bureau, together with the association, convened a hearing. At that time, the representatives of both parties were still able to reach an agreement. Later, it was decided to convene a mediation on the 12th of the same month. However, the representative of the employer stated that the company's directors had left Shanghai and had not returned, so he requested a postponement. The mediation was rescheduled for the 15th. As the oral replies of the representatives of both parties were not clear enough, the chairman of the mediation committee ordered both parties to submit written replies separately and immediately sent personnel to both parties the next day to urge them to submit their reports. This is the mediation process for the issue of the company's workers requesting a salary increase. However, the company's Vehicle Department workers suddenly went on strike yesterday morning, gathering crowds, coercing, and besieging the company's manager, refusing to accept advice. When the police team arrived to maintain order, there were criminals throwing bombs and injuring people. Such outrageous actions are extremely hateful. However, the riot yesterday showed that there were bad elements instigating it from the middle. The association and the government are deeply concerned that the company's workers will be instigated by them and innocently implicated. In addition to issuing a general order to strictly arrest the leaders and investigate them according to the law, we urgently issue a joint announcement ordering the company's workers to comply with it and uniformly restore the original state before 12:00 noon on the 20th. If they dare to disobey, the employer will be allowed to dismiss them and recruit new workers. Do not hesitate and delay, or you will mislead yourselves. The salary increase issue will still be the responsibility of the Social Bureau, together with the association, to actively mediate in order to resolve it as soon as possible. Each of you must abide by this and not neglect it.

▲ Board Meeting: After General Manager Lu Bohong was rescued, he reported the incident to the board of directors. The International Relations Research Association Welcomes Dr. Gu Ziren 120

The International Relations Research Association held a general meeting of all members at the Bank Club at 5:00 PM on the 18th to welcome Dr. Gu Ziren. Chairman Chen Liting delivered an opening speech, and then Dr. Gu reported on the situation in the United States, saying: "The last time I went abroad was at the invitation of the American Williamstown Justitue of politics to attend the association's lectures. When I arrived at Williamstown, the association had already held it for two days. There was still no representative from our country at this meeting. Those who attended the political association were all members. The lecture time was in the evening, and the main topics were (1) the Sino-Japanese issue (2) the world economic issue. My attendance was specifically for the Northeast issue. There were six or seven Japanese representatives. Dr. Nitobe took turns hosting members every night. It can be seen that the Japanese attach importance to publicity. In terms of topics, Chinese representatives talked about the entire Chinese issue, Japanese representatives talked about the entire Japanese issue, and Dr. Nitobe's lectures were mostly taken from Japanese warlords. People said that the political association's meeting was almost entirely for Chinese publicity. On the positive side, I promoted it; on the negative side, the Japanese insulted China and tried to cover up their atrocities. The more they tried to cover it up, the more they revealed it, giving the Americans a considerable understanding of the Sino-Japanese issue. The Japanese representatives in the United States had various assistance, and the speakers had secretaries to assist them, but I was alone. Although I was not completely isolated, I encountered various difficulties. It is undeniable that the Japanese lectures had prepared drafts in advance, but because I had no one to help, I had to speak impromptu. However, if I did not deliver the original manuscript to the reporters after the lecture, they would often misunderstand the original intention and publish it in the newspaper. This is the difficulty I deeply felt. The arguments made by the Japanese at the political association that were not made in the past were (1) China is an unorganized country (2) China only has a few thousand years of ancient culture. Therefore, China and Japan have different international statuses, so Japan cannot be held responsible for destroying the Washington Treaty in this conflict. Dr. Nitobe also had an argument, denouncing the Chinese as an inferior race in the world. When the Japanese army occupied the Northeast, the Chinese never showed any resistance, and then sought help from other countries. In fact, the decadent spirit of the Chinese has been passed down for thousands of years. When the Japanese did evil, the New York Times did not say a word. When there was civil war in China, it publicized it, saying that civil war had broken out everywhere in China, proving that China was unorganized and unsystematic. This kind of publicity had a great influence on the psychology of the Americans." In addition to attending the Williamstown Political Association, Gu also went to more than 90 public and private organizations in other parts of the United States to give lectures.

The Feixing Patrol Ship Has Been Inspected and Accepted Yesterday 126

Given the weakness of the existing police boat force at the Jianghai Customs, a request was approved to order two 500-ton patrol ships from the Jiangnan Shipyard by the former Customs Commissioner Zhang Fuyun. They were named Huaxing and Feixing. The Huaxing was completed and delivered for customs use a month ago. The Feixing was also completed on the 15th of this month. Sudden Assassination of Red Swastika Society Official 128

▲ Zhou Zhiyuan Seems to Have No Enemies

▲ Two Men Commit the Heinous Crime

▲ An Unfamiliar Guest Behaving Suspiciously

▲ What Was Discussed During the Two-Hour Conversation?

Zhou Zhiyuan, a native of Wuchang, Hubei, was 47 years old and resided at No. 1046, Lane 2, Siwen Li, Datong Road, Xinzha Road in Shanghai. He previously worked as an inspector at Jardine Matheson in Nanjing. However, due to poor business conditions, he was laid off. After arriving in Shanghai, he was introduced by a friend to work as a general affairs officer and accountant at the Shanghai General Office of the Southeast Branch of the China World Red Swastika Society at No. 7 Danshui Road, earning a monthly salary of $30. According to staff members of the society, Zhou was very amiable and harmonious with his colleagues. He was also very frugal, taking care of all matters at home, big and small. Around 8:30 AM yesterday, Zhou got up as usual and went to the market to buy vegetables. Shortly after returning home, his wife, Zhou Wang, 29 years old and a native of Wuchang, was still asleep. As Zhou stepped onto the steps of the back door and used his key to open the door, two men, about 30 to 40 years old, suddenly chased after him and fired two shots at him with handguns. One shot hit the ground, and the other entered Zhou's left ear and exited through the top of his right head. Zhou immediately fell to the ground. The murderers, seeing that their goal had been achieved, turned and fled. Zhou's second landlord heard the noise and came out to see Zhou lying stiff in a pool of blood. He quickly went upstairs to wake up Zhou's wife and immediately reported to the police station. At 9:15 AM, Zhou was taken to Baolong Hospital by ambulance for treatment. However, due to his serious injuries, he died at 9:35 AM. The police station sent the body to the Fielun Road morgue for examination and dispatched personnel to investigate the scene of the incident and to strictly apprehend the murderers. According to staff members of the Red Swastika Society office, Zhou rarely had social interactions with outsiders. However, two fellow villagers of Zhou visited him at the society the day before. They spoke in their local dialect, so no one knew what they were discussing. They talked for over two hours before leaving. Zhou even saw them off at the door. Colleagues at the society found the actions of these two guests quite strange.

Two Dollars to Inlay a Gold Tooth: A Naive Girl Is Deceived 129

▲ Seventy-Nine Dollars and Trinkets Taken Away

▲ The Pancake Shop Owner Is Delightfully Happy

▲ After Strict Interrogation by the Indigenous Detective

▲ The Truth Is Revealed, Joy Turns to Sorrow

Ni Yazi, a woman from Yangzhou, is 28 years old and of average appearance. She lives near No. 2125, Fulu Li, Yangshupu Road, where her fellow villager Zhao Xiang (22 years old) runs a pancake shop. Ni often visits the shop to buy pancakes and has known Zhao for a long time. Recently, seeing that Ni's emotions were developing, Zhao enticed her in every possible way, hoping to fulfill his desires. On the 1st of this month, Zhao told Ni that he wanted to become her lover and would first give her two silver dollars to inlay a gold tooth as a token of his sincerity. Ni took the money home. Her father, Ni Yuanlong, and mother found out and asked about the source of the money. Ni, embarrassed, could not answer and was scolded. Ni told Zhao the truth. After Zhao and Ni discussed the matter, Zhao instructed Ni to take the opportunity to steal valuables and bring them to his shop. Then, he would take her to his house on Zhujiabang Road, Yangshupu, to live together and avoid parental control. Since Ni Yazi was not Ni Yuanlong's biological daughter but an adopted daughter at the age of two, Ni Yazi was pleased to hear this. On the afternoon of the 3rd, she secretly stole seventy-nine dollars in cash, gold rings, and other items and took them to Zhao's shop. Together, they rode to an unmarked flat on Zhujiabang Road. That night, at 8 PM, Zhao defiled Ni Yazi, treating her as his wife. After Ni Yazi disappeared, her father, Ni Yuanlong, found out that the aforementioned items were missing. He asked people to search for her everywhere, but there was no news. He then reported to the Yangshupu police station. After several days without any progress, he placed an advertisement in the newspaper with a clear description of his daughter's age, figure, clothing, and photograph, seeking her whereabouts. Zhao Xiang, upon reading the newspaper, knew that he could not hide for long and worried about being caught. He instructed Ni to surrender herself to the police station the day before, falsely claiming that she had run away from home after being scolded by her parents and had been staying with a girlfriend in Pudong. She claimed she now wished to return home and requested that a detective be sent to escort her back. However, the Chinese detective Wang Jinsheng, an experienced investigator, knew that Ni's words were not true. After interrogating her strictly, Ni told the whole truth. Wang Jinsheng immediately reported to the police chief and, along with a foreign detective, secretly went to the pancake shop and arrested Zhao Xiang, taking him into custody. Ni was sent back to the Ni family. Yesterday morning, the police station escorted Zhao to the Third Criminal Tribunal of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin described the details of the case, stating that the defendant should be punished according to Article 370, paragraph 3 of the Criminal Code for intimidating and defrauding. However, although the defendant denied sending the threatening letters received by the victim, whether or not he was the perpetrator still needed to be determined through handwriting analysis and investigation of evidence. Therefore, a postponement was requested. Ni Yuanlong then testified about the circumstances of receiving the letters. When Zhao Xiang was questioned, he confessed that he was married but was not on good terms with his wife. He claimed that Ni Yazi had run away to his house to stay temporarily. He claimed his mother informed him at the shop, and he returned home and told her to go home, but she refused. She said she had a relationship with his younger brother and had previously asked a matchmaker to seek marriage, but her father did not agree. He claimed that her allegations of him giving her two silver dollars, inlaying a gold tooth, and spending the night together were completely false. Judge Shen Bingrong ordered the defendant to be detained pending further investigation. The reporter then asked Ni why she had committed suicide and who the Miss ○○ (withheld to prevent further complications) mentioned in the letter was. The reply was that the so-called Miss ○○ was named Xue. They were classmates at Zhoulin Elementary School in Zhangjiabang. He was very affectionate towards her and wanted to marry her, but she did not reciprocate. Now that she has married someone else, he committed suicide. Zhou Changming can be described as a single-minded lover who suffers from unrequited love.

Russian News Agency Employee Suspected of Extortion 130

▲ Wu Zhangsheng's Sister Seeks Inheritance

▲ Zhang Tongzhao Suddenly Arrives to Mediate

▲ Admits to Writing Anonymous Letters

▲ Extortion Letters Still Under Investigation

Wu Zhangsheng, a local resident residing at No. 36, Maqi Road, Yidaojiao, Huaxi, owns a substantial ancestral estate. In addition to his wife and children, he also has a younger sister named Mituo, who is still unmarried. In the summer of this year, Mituo suddenly abandoned her sister-in-law and fled alone, her whereabouts unknown. After several days, she returned home on her own accord. Wu Zhangsheng did not investigate the matter thoroughly at the time. One day, an unexpected guest arrived at the Wu's residence, claiming to be Zhang Tongzhao. He claimed that Mituo's goddaughter was her close friend and that he had learned that Mituo wanted to divide the inheritance with her sister-in-law. Therefore, he came to visit Wu Zhangsheng to mediate and avoid litigation. Wu Zhangsheng was out on that day, so his wife, Wang, briefly interacted with Zhang. Zhang left a note before leaving, firmly instructing Wang to hand it to Zhangsheng. Several days later, Zhang continued to visit but only met Wang, who claimed that her husband did not want to meet with him to discuss family affairs. Zhang's two attempts were unsuccessful and met with rebuffs, so he left dejectedly and never visited again. He immediately hired two lawyers on behalf of Mituo and filed a lawsuit against Wu Zhangsheng, seeking a division of the inheritance, requesting a separation of 100,000 yuan, with the contract stipulating that half would be taken as a reward. Having been sued, Zhangsheng decided to wait quietly for the legal resolution. Unexpectedly, on the 14th of last month, a letter was delivered by the postman. Upon opening it, the language was extremely fierce, demanding 20,000 yuan to be paid between 5 and 6 PM on the 17th of this month at the Ningbo Hall on Minguo Road in the French Concession. The person going there would be identified by holding two rolls of woolen yarn. Wu sent the letter to the Geden Road police station for investigation. The police chief immediately sent detective Liu Chunshu to the Ningbo Hall on the appointed date with other detectives to wait. After waiting all day, there was no sign of anyone. On the 19th of last month, Wu received another threatening letter with similar wording, but the amount demanded was reduced to 5,000 yuan, and it was agreed that the meeting would still be at the Ningbo Hall the next day. However, when Detective Liu went there at the appointed time, he still returned empty-handed. Since then, Wu had not received any more letters of this kind. Unexpectedly, at the beginning of this month, Wu received an anonymous letter stating that if he wanted to resolve the matter of his sister's request to divide the property, he could contact Zhang Tongzhao. Wu ignored it after reading it. On the 12th, a second anonymous letter arrived, continuing to mention the division of property and adding that if he wanted to know who wrote the letter, he could check the note left in July. Only then did Wu realize that these letters were actually written by Zhang Tongzhao. Therefore, he began investigating Zhang's address. The day before, he discovered that Zhang was also a local resident living at No. 74 Guanyinge Street, Xinkaihe, and was now working as a clerk at a certain Russian news agency at No. 19 Bowuyuan Road. Therefore, he reported the matter to the Geden Road police station, which sent detective Liu to arrest Zhang at his home but found no one. He then went to the news agency and arrested Zhang, taking him into custody for questioning. Zhang only admitted that he had written the two anonymous letters, one by asking his friend Ding to write it and the other by writing it himself. He also admitted that he wrote the note left at Wu's house. He denied sending the two threatening letters that Wu had received. Yesterday morning, the police station brought Wu Zhangsheng and his wife to the First Special District District Court to be interrogated by Judge Wu Zhen. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang described the case and stated that the defendant should be punished according to Article 370, paragraph 3 of the Criminal Code for intimidation and fraud. However, although the defendant denied the threatening letters received by the victim, whether or not he was the perpetrator still needed to be determined through handwriting analysis and investigation of evidence, so a postponement was requested. Wu Zhangsheng then described the circumstances of receiving the letters. When Zhang Tongzhao was questioned, he stated that the anonymous letters he wrote were to persuade the plaintiff to reconcile with his sister and that the 50% reward was lawyer's fees. He claimed that although he hired a lawyer, he had no selfish motives. Judge Wu then ordered the defendant to be detained for handwriting analysis and further interrogation.

Wang Boqun Submits Document to Central Government Regarding Yongnian Earth Transport Case 135

▲If There is Concrete Evidence of Trafficking, I Will Accept Guilt

▲Requests the Central Executive Committee to Uphold Justice

Former Minister of Communications Wang Boqun submitted a document to the Central Party Headquarters regarding the Yongnian earth transport case, stating: "Submitting this document regarding the Yongnian earth transport case, which has unexpectedly led to unfair criticism, directly damaging my personal reputation and indirectly affecting the dignity of the Party and the nation. I earnestly request you to uphold justice to clarify the truth. I, Boqun, was ordered in June of this year to inspect Sichuan, traveling for three months, and only in early September did I complete my official duties and return east. At that time, my mother was ill, and I was eager to return home. Since the Yongnian ship was faster and there was no need to transfer along the way, I boarded the ship on the 8th with my entourage from Chongqing. Because I needed to report the inspection results to Chairman Chiang, I planned to disembark in Hankou. At the beginning of the voyage, I heard rumors that someone was taking this opportunity to smuggle opium. Since opium was almost openly traded in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River and Chongqing was a gathering place for special goods from the Southwest, and also a place of morphine production, merchants paid taxes to transport and sell it, and every ship carried it. Moreover, there were special officials to investigate and arrest smugglers, so there was no need to overstep my duties. However, I warned my entourage to conduct themselves with integrity and ordered them to inspect every checkpoint. On the 10th, many cases of passengers smuggling were discovered. On the 11th, when I and my entourage disembarked in Hankou after inspecting our luggage, the local special tax office seized a large quantity of opium and morphine on the ship. I immediately asked Chairman Chiang to investigate the matter strictly, stating that although the waters were connected, the clean and dirty were distinct, and those who sought personal gain should be warned. Although I once worked with Shuangqing, he was now an official in Guizhou Province. He was ill when I left Chongqing, and his wife had a strong addiction, which was well known. However, whether there was opium or morphine in his luggage was difficult to interfere with, even though we were on the same ship, as he was not under my command. These were the facts at the time, but the public, not understanding the truth, made wild speculations based on my old relationship with Shuangqing. Local newspapers also exaggerated the rumors and deliberately defamed me. However, I believed that although public opinion could confuse the audience for a time, the truth would eventually come out after Chairman Chiang ordered the relevant authorities to investigate impartially. I did not have time to refute each and every unfair accusation. Unexpectedly, the Beijing Municipal Party Headquarters also picked up rumors and accused me of trafficking in opium in a resolution opposing the public sale of opium, which was shocking. On October 31st, the Central Daily News, the propaganda organ of our party, also used ambiguous words to subtly criticize me. I have followed the Prime Minister in the revolution for more than twenty years and have confidence in my personal conduct. I have sacrificed myself in many situations, regardless of gains or losses. I have served in the central government for many years and have seen the chaos of factions within the party, which is not a sign of political prosperity. I have always adhered to the principle of treating people with kindness, not flattering or being opportunistic in order to seek political purity. This has led to a concentration of resentment. I have been slandered and defamed many times over the years. Since our party came to power, times have been difficult and the nation has been plagued by many problems. Political enemies outside the party have conspired to subvert us, and malicious slander has been rampant, leaving no stone unturned in discrediting and alienating our party cadres. Since my honor and disgrace are closely linked to the party and the government, they have taken this opportunity to insinuate and attack me, directly damaging my personal reputation and indirectly insulting the dignity of the party and the government. Their poisonous schemes are not surprising. However, the party headquarters at all levels are the branches of our party, and the Central Daily News is the mouthpiece of our party. I believe that our comrades who serve in the party headquarters at all levels and in the Central Daily News should take a stand based on their position and use fair arguments and a calm attitude to seek the truth based on the facts in order to silence the slanderers and maintain the prestige of the party and the government. However, the Beijing Municipal Party Headquarters and the Central Daily News have not done this, repeating what others have said. Not only are they harming each other, but they are also helping the enemy and making those close to us angry and those who hate us happy. This is truly a cause for weeping over party discipline and morality. Moreover, in terms of the case, the place where the trafficking originated was Chongqing, and the place where it was discovered was Hankou. It is not difficult to know whether I am involved. Opium has always been openly traded in Chongqing. Who bought it and who sold it at that time? Once investigated, the truth will be revealed. Also, whether there are special markings on the boxes and luggage seized in Hankou that belong to me personally, and whether the detainees have made any confessions involving me, the party headquarters in each place can easily make a judgment. Furthermore, in terms of law, there are clear provisions against fabricating facts with the intention of damaging the reputation of others. Without concrete evidence, personal opinions should not be used to arbitrarily slander. Moreover, some say that I have inherited the legacy of my ancestors and can afford to live a comfortable life. I have always saved money and worked hard for public welfare. I am not like someone living in an empty house, so desperate that I would choose any means. There are many ways to make money; why would I risk my personal reputation and violate the law for such a profit? Even if we take a step back and assume that I intended to traffic in opium, I could have contacted the specialized authorities beforehand to facilitate passage. Why would I have been caught halfway and even ordered the checkpoints to inspect as if nothing had happened? A little investigation into this matter will reveal the truth. If we must judge others based on worldly preferences, then how can there be anyone in the world who cherishes their own integrity? In short, the Beijing Municipal Party Headquarters and the Central Daily News, ignorant of the facts and interests, and without investigating the case and the truth, have made arbitrary decisions and unfounded comments. Not only am I personally being defamed, but the party and the nation are also being implicated. After careful consideration, I cannot remain silent. I am submitting this document detailing the circumstances of the case and my personal feelings, earnestly requesting your council to uphold justice and clarify the truth. If there is concrete evidence that I have engaged in trafficking or acted for personal gain, I will accept guilt and submit myself to the sanctions of the law and party discipline. Otherwise, if I am innocent and have been unfairly accused, then the Beijing Municipal Party Headquarters and the Central Daily News should bear corresponding responsibility. I will accept your judgment on how to correct or admonish them. I have poured out my heart and anxiously await your orders. Furthermore, I have returned from Sichuan and have traveled through mountains and rivers. My old illness has relapsed. Once I have recovered, I will return to Beijing to attend meetings. Respectfully submitted to the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang. Wang Boqun."

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to Municipal Council Urging Swift Resolution of Telephone Price Increase Issue 137

▲Prevent the Use of Coercive Measures to Achieve Unilateral Benefits

▲Please Adopt the Six Proposals Made by Taxpayers

The taxpayers of the Public Concession recently sent a letter to the Chinese Taxpayers' Association, outlining six major reasons why the Municipal Council should be approached to negotiate the issue of telephone price increases, in order to reach a swift resolution. Key excerpts from the document are as follows:

▲Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to Municipal Council. Yesterday, the Taxpayers' Association sent a letter to the Municipal Council, stating: "We have received letters from the First District Branch of the Shanghai Citizens' United Association and the Nanjing Business Community United Association, stating that our members Sanxing Factory (telephone 94834), Hefeng Hao (telephone 94944), Shichangtai Hao (telephone 94798), Maoshenghe Hao (telephone 94717), and Changfeng Hao (telephone 94683) have reported that their telephone bills have either been paid at the old price for the autumn and winter seasons or have not been paid pending resolution of the price increase negotiations. However, on November 13th, the Shanghai Telephone Company cut off their lines, rendering their telephones unusable. They request that our association advocate for them." "Upon investigation, our association, representing the majority of its members, maintains that the price should not be increased excessively. We have outlined the reasons in a letter to your council, urging you to advocate for them. Our association hopes that 'the company will cancel the price increase and establish a fair price, taking into account the interests of both parties and seeking a compromise that is suitable for all.' We originally hoped to resolve the dispute and put an end to it as soon as possible. However, the company has ignored this intention and has not given it any consideration. It is now resorting to unreasonable disconnection measures. Its sole justification is that it has been approved by the Municipal Council, so it dares to pressure users and become more and more aggressive, doing whatever it wants and disregarding everything. It is even cutting off the lines of users who have already paid the old price for the autumn and winter seasons, which is even more contrary to commercial ethics. We fear that if this stalemate continues, there will be no positive outcome. If users who have been disconnected experience a fire during this period and suffer unlimited losses due to their inability to use the telephone, who will be responsible? This matter concerns social peace and public communication. We are writing to you again to request that you investigate and provide prompt assistance, etc." Furthermore, Shao Renhua wrote, stating that "recently, the Shanghai Telephone Company suddenly increased prices and retroactively charged for past bills, causing opposition from Chinese and foreign users, who have successively requested that your council protest repeatedly. It is said that justice has not been completely extinguished and that the company, considering the situation and reflecting on its actions, should eventually seek a peaceful solution. I have used the telephone in my home for nearly twenty years and have always paid my bills promptly. I have never complained about the lack of service. This time, I am facing this unexpected situation and share the same feelings as other users. I have been questioned and criticized, so it is naturally inappropriate to remain silent. Before a resolution is reached, I have repeatedly paid the original amount without receiving a receipt and have temporarily adopted a wait-and-see attitude. Given my long-standing status as a good customer, I cannot rashly use pressure and harmful measures to satisfy the notion of might makes right. Otherwise, it would be like someone with the power of life and death arbitrarily punishing someone with death for the slightest dissatisfaction. Last Wednesday, I suddenly received a letter from the company, not only not returning the receipt but also demanding that I pay the new fee within four months or face disconnection and a reinstallation fee of twelve taels. Left with no choice, I planned to pay the new fee but temporarily refused to pay the retroactive amount. As a result, the telephone in my home is now silent. I anticipate that many other users will face the same treatment and will be forced to pay. For the sake of the whole, I can only ask your council or other associations to make a final protest and make a responsible plea. According to reason, even the new fee should be notified two months in advance) so that this matter can be brought to a fair conclusion and prevent society from being in constant turmoil. Otherwise, please announce a plan so that everyone can follow it (or next time, let everyone refuse to pay and have their phones removed together to resist. After all, decades ago, people lived and worked in peace without telephones. Moreover, the market is now so depressed). I have the following questions and hope that your council will consider whether they are viable, which would be very fortunate, etc." and attached ㈠ whether the telephone users all have contracts with the telephone company, and whether the so-called contract contains equality and the meaning of mutual agreement, and at least the principle of public judgment in case of incidents as in other contracts; ㈡ whether the company, even if it has a contract with the user, can rashly increase the price without first seeking consent and notification, and can retroactively charge electricity fees for more than three months in the past because it has not achieved its desired purpose and regardless of whether the user can afford it; ㈢ if this retroactive recognition becomes a reality, then if the company needs to add income due to expenses or miscalculations affecting the business situation, whether the retroactive establishment or even the need for as many as thirteen months will be followed by users as well; ㈣ whether the user has the right to use the telephone if the original price is paid before the contract is legally canceled, or whether the company can arbitrarily increase the surcharge and immediately stop the service and remove the electrical equipment, making the user submit one by one; ㈤ if the company’s issuance of orders is so dictatorial, what rights do users hold in the contract and what does the meaning of it all mean, and can a public exclusive undertaking do whatever it wants, and will all other contracts lose their effect; ㈥ if the improvement of equipment increases the cost of assets and the income should also increase, it is undeniable, but whether it needs to be recovered in the long term and gradually, or whether the company holds the power of calculation and control to the extreme degree; The association has repeatedly informed your director of the telephone price increase dispute and requested the board of directors to reconsider it. Before the board of directors has reconsidered and decided, your director should prevent the telephone company from using the high-pressure means approved by your bureau, which is still opposed by taxpayers, to violate the unilateral interests, and the lack of careful measures has led to this increasingly complex problem, and the association is very worried about it, and it may be possible for the company users to cause mutual inconvenience, and the director is responsible for solving the problem in view of the association’s view of the civil society joint association and the nanyang road business circle united association, and please your director to explain each of shao renhua’s questions one by one so as to turn over the correspondence to be handled.

▲Bei Zuyi Sends Letter to Taxpayers' Association. Accountant Bei Zuyi sent a letter to the Shanghai Public Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association, stating: "I am writing to you to report on a conversation I had with Mr. Zhong, the director-general of the Municipal Council, regarding the telephone price increase issue. I visited him at 10:00 AM on November 16th, accompanied by Mr. He Dequi, the council's representative. I have summarized the contents of the conversation below: Mr. Zhong first reported on the situation of the telephone company since it took over the China and Foreign Telephone Company, stating briefly that the telephone price increase was due to the Municipal Council accepting the telephone company's report. When the company took over the China and Foreign Telephone Company in 1929, Mr. Anson calculated that the telephone price should be increased by 25% immediately based on the company's economic situation. After careful consideration by the Municipal Council's board of directors and the Public Utilities Committee, it was determined that it could not be maintained without a price increase, and all the people on the board of directors and the Public Utilities Committee, including foreigners, had deeply studied it through Chinese and foreign lawyers. At that time, the telephone company voluntarily waited until the automatic telephone was completed before increasing the price. Now that the work within the boundary has been completed, it can be increased in accordance with the contract. This matter has been handled through legal procedures and is not Mr. Zhong's individual proposal. Recently, the telephone company has reported that from the time it took over to the end of March of this year, it lost a total of 218,432 yuan in regulations, and it is estimated that it will lose a total of 242,000 yuan in regulations by next year (with a copy of the original letter given by Zhong Sijun attached). Regarding the issue of building roads and installing lines across the boundary, a contract has now been signed with the Shanghai Municipal Government. Those who build roads across the boundary must pay the Municipal Government 12 yuan per user per year, and those who do not build roads across the boundary in the Chinese boundary must pay 60 yuan per user per year, and must also pay the Ministry of Communications 12,000 yuan in regulations per year. The telephone company is willing to bear the cost of this payment so that the telephone charges inside and outside the boundary are the same. This loss can only be added to the telephone rate, otherwise, how can the telephone company maintain itself?" (Zu Yi said) "The law is not retroactive, not only Chinese law but also all countries' laws. This should be noted." (Zhong Sijun said) "I personally feel that this layer is not very appropriate, but it has been thoroughly researched by the telephone company's Municipal Council lawyers and is considered to be no problem." (Zu Yi said) "Since Mr. Anson proposed to increase the price rate in 1929, why not do it at that time? At that time, the social and economic situation was different from the present, or it would not be as difficult as it is today. Now it seems that it is not the time to release this when the social economy is in a very depressed state. Has the telephone company made public the company's situation as described by Zhong Sijun? Now the Chinese side has not learned, so the telephone company must let the users understand the company's situation before they can cooperate. Even if you must increase the price rate, you should invite representatives from the Municipal Council, the telephone company, and the users to consult and discuss the methods. The telephone company and the users have an original contract, and the expenses that the users should bear are specified in the contract, and the contract is signed by both parties. The telephone company's price increase is a unilateral claim and did not notify the users in advance. This layer is still not in line with the general procedures." (Zhong Sijun said) "The telephone company's only income is telephone bills. If the telephone company cannot maintain its cost, how can it serve the users? Like a store's goods, there must be a cost calculation to determine the selling price. It cannot force the store to sell the goods at a loss just because the buyer's economic strength is weak. Now the telephone company's income is not enough to cover the cost, so there is no way to pay ordinary dividends. If this is the case, who would be willing to invest again? There will be no one to run this telephone business and there will be no telephone supply within the boundary. If the Municipal Council takes it over and runs it itself, where will the Municipal Council get this funding and cannot afford this loss? At that time, it is still a matter of tax increases for the people. This is a matter of fact and cannot be forced. As for the telephone company's situation, it has been announced one after another or has not paid attention." (Zu Yi said) "Telephones are a public undertaking and are exclusive, so they cannot be compared with other profit-making businesses." Zhong Sijun did not answer this question. (Zu Yi said) "Today's newspaper reported that the telephone company has started to cut lines. Please pay special attention to this, for fear of unexpected unfortunate incidents." Zhong Sijun replied that this matter should be noted. The above conversation is related to the telephone price increase issue. Other ordinary polite words will not be repeated. But Zu Yi

Page 16

still has opinions, but because of the time it has been a long time, each other's things are tight and can not fully express, I had to resign and leave. Because it is related to public interests, I will specially return the summarized situation and hope to check it out for reference and easy to solve.

Second Special Court Burns Narcotics 140

The Shanghai Second Special District Court, from July to the end of September of this year, confiscated narcotics such as opium, morphine, and red pills, as well as gambling items from cases resolved by the French Concession Police. The fourth burning was scheduled for yesterday afternoon. The Ministry of Justice Administration and the Third High Branch Court were notified in advance, and the military, political, police, and judicial organs in Shanghai were sent separate letters to send representatives to supervise the scene. The details have been reported in the previous report. The Logistics Section hired workers to build a reed shed on the vacant lot next to the court in the east and arranged the site. Yesterday morning, Feng Meixue, director of the Stolen Goods Section, ordered the workers to move all the narcotics and gambling items to the site and arrange them one by one. There were a total of 826 cases of opium, morphine, red pills, and smoking paraphernalia. In addition, the four cases from the previous session that were appealed and not yet finalized were also included. Representatives from various organs in Shanghai who arrived at the scene included Li Zeng from the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, Ma Mingchu from the Municipal Government, Lu Youchang from the Jianghai Customs Superintendent's Office, Ren Bin from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Jin Yuxi from the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, Wu Fengwen from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Hang Dingan from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, Sun Zhixing from the Second High Branch Court, Tang Zaili from the Third High Branch Court, Lin Xichou from the Prosecutor's Office of the Third High Branch Court, Ju Zhijing from the Shanghai First Special Court, Zhang Yaoguang from the Prosecutor's Office of the First Special Court, (French name, phonetic transliteration) from the French Concession Police Department, and representatives from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Lawyers' Association.

After arriving at the court, they were received by Court President Shen Xiqing, Chief Prosecutor Chen Beisan, and Chief Clerk Xiao Jinfang. Then, clerks Wei Yuwei, Wang Baoxun, and Ren Qiwu supervised the workers to open and inspect the various narcotics, weigh them, and carry them to the center of the site, where they were piled with firewood and kerosene for ignition. Adding salt to the fire caused black smoke to rise and a foul odor to fill the air.

After the narcotics were burned, the gambling items were burned until the evening. The representatives left one after another. The narcotics burned this time included 1,771 opium pipes, red pill pipes, and other accessories. There were also about 300 catties of opium, hundreds of pounds of red pills, morphine, heroin, cocaine, and copper, ceramic, and glass utensils used to manufacture narcotics. The gambling items included 817 sheets of flower lottery tickets, mahjong, poker, pencils, abacuses, and other items.

Citizens' Movement for Rent Reduction on North Jiangxi Road 142

The 26th District Branch of the Municipal Federation of Associations reported that more than 50 households, including those in the Fanzhi, Rongsheng, and Gengfu Lane residences, Zida, Honglou, and Guangchengli, and other residents of North Jiangxi Road, requested rent reductions because the road construction has not been completed and the post-war environment is harsh, resulting in empty houses, few people, and a sluggish business market, making it very difficult for shops to maintain their livelihoods. Therefore, they jointly requested the landlord, the Far East Company, to reduce rents to help the market. The association convened a temporary meeting of members from North Jiangxi Road at 8:00 PM yesterday. More than 100 people attended, including Wang Binpei, Ye Rongji, Tang Guansong, Zhuo Biye, Lu Ping, Gong Huimin, Zhou Kun, Li Guanglin, Xu Xianhua, Liang Chunlin, Wu Zhong'an, Ou Yuehua, Zhang Bingji, Tong Hongyuan, Wang Yuchen, Gui Tang, Zhao Guangyu, and Li Changzhao Ganyu. Zhu Muye, Ni Yangzhou, and Zheng Dongshan were elected as the presidium. After the report was completed, the following resolutions were passed: ㈠ The rent for Fanzhi, Rongsheng, and Gengfu Lane will be calculated from the date of completion of the road construction. ㈡ Due to the sluggish market and the difficulty of maintaining shops, a 30% rent reduction is requested. ㈢ Before the rent reduction is resolved, the rent will be deposited in the bank. ㈣ Zheng Dongshan and Zhu Muye were appointed as representatives to negotiate with the landlord. ㈤ Yu Hualong and Chao Kun were hired as legal advisors. ㈥ The party, government, and other organizations of the Municipal Federation of Associations were requested to uphold justice. ㈦ Wang Yuchen, Liang Chunlin, Gong Huimin, and 10 others were appointed as members of the rent discussion committee. ㈧ The patrol donation issue will be paid after the road is completed, and a letter will be sent to the donation office to discuss it. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

The Shengshun Li Housing Association Negotiates Rent Reduction Without Success 143

▲ Landlords Insist on Differentiating Between New and Old Tenants

The tenants of Shengshun Li, Baoshan Road, Zhabei, suffered substantial losses due to the January 28th Incident. After the agreement was reached, most of the original tenants moved back in. A small number of tenants, for special reasons, did not return and sublet to relatives and friends. Shengshun Company, the management company of the area, disregarded the suffering of those who had survived the looting and took the opportunity to oppress them, coercively increasing rents twofold and charging a monthly "small rent" (which old tenants could avoid). The tenants of the area, citing the rent reduction examples in various places after the war, believed that rents should be appropriately reduced, but instead they were doubled, which they could not afford. They collectively decided to demand that the landlords reduce rents by 20% of the original price. A delegation appointed by the association went to negotiate the other day, but to no avail. The landlords requested that new and old tenants be distinguished first, before further negotiations could take place. They stated that new tenants had agreed beforehand and had contractual relationships, so they could not be discussed together, while old tenants might be open to discussion due to their long-standing relationship. After careful discussion by the association's executive committee, it was determined that since there was no distinction between new and old houses in the area, the rent prices should not have any distinction. They jointly decided to notify all tenants to deposit their rent in the bank starting from November, to prevent the landlords from using rent arrears as an excuse for long-term demands. The letter from the association to the landlords reads as follows: Respectfully, according to the report from our association representatives Zhou Qibin and Yang Lisan, who were ordered to go to negotiate with you regarding the rent reduction issue in this area, the situation has been brought to the meeting. After deliberation by the ad hoc executive committee, it was resolved that since there is no distinction between new and old houses in this area, the rent prices should not have any distinction. This kind of proposition is absolutely unacceptable. The proposition to coercively increase rent twofold amidst the voices for rent reduction after the war is even more against the trend of the times and is not allowed by the facts and reasons. In short, the tenants of this area should enjoy equal treatment. Before the rent dispute is resolved, each tenant will pay 80% of the original pre-war price starting from November and deposit it monthly into the Shanghai Bank on the boundary road, to prevent anyone from using rent arrears as an excuse for long-term demands. The association has been responsible for notifying accordingly and recording the case, submitted for your review and processing, which is in the public interest.

Shun'an Li Tenants on Changchun Road Petition 144

The residents of Shun'an Li on Changchun Road, Zhabei, fled during the Shanghai battle, as the area was under Japanese influence. After the Public Security Bureau moved back to its original location in mid-June, the tenants also moved back. However, there were few residents and business had not recovered. Now, the landlord, Chen Shunji, believed that the tenants' request for a five-month rent exemption and an eight-month rent reduction was difficult to accommodate. Therefore, the Shun'an Li Tenants' Autonomous Association reported all the hardships and the landlord's coercion to move out to the municipal government, requesting a fair resolution.

Dr. Ling Qihan Practices Law 148

Dr. Ling Qihan was a top student at the former Aurora University. In 1926, he went to Europe to study law for five years. He obtained a doctorate in law from the Capital University of Belgium, a master's degree in maritime law, and a master's degree in political diplomacy from the University of Leuven. Last year, he returned to China after completing his studies. He was hired by Shenbao to write commentaries and later founded the Shenbao Monthly and served as a professor at Soochow Law School. Now, Mr. Ling plans to use his spare time from writing and teaching to serve the society and has partnered with Yao Zhaoli, a famous lawyer in Shanghai, to form the Zhonghe Law Firm on the third floor of Zhonghe Bank on Nanjing Road and Shanxi Road to handle civil and criminal litigation and non-litigation matters. It is heard that Mr. Ling and Mr. Yao are both from prominent families in Shanghai and will definitely uphold justice and protect human rights for all circles in Shanghai.

A Man Borrows a Car 151

▲ Dalong Driver Stands on Zhongshan Road

▲ Three People Board the Car and Speed Away

At about 7:40 AM yesterday, an unknown man suddenly came to the Dalong Motor Company on North Henan Road in the Public Concession and claimed that he wanted to hire a car to visit a friend. The company ordered driver Zang Shengcai (34 years old, Ningbo native) to drive a sedan with Public Concession white license plate No. 18138. The man sat in the car and told the driver to drive to Zhongshan Road in western Shanghai. The driver started the engine and sped west. When he reached a remote place near Daxia University on Zhongshan Road, three people stood there. The man in the car ordered the driver to stop. The man jumped out of the car and rushed up with the three people. Two of them each held a pistol and dragged the driver down first. The other two jumped into the car, started the engine, and sped away, watching the driver stand on the roadside and not allowing him to make a sound. After about two hours, he was released and walked away. The driver, realizing that the car had been robbed without a trace, immediately ran to the Sixth District Police Station and the Jing'an Temple Patrol Room to report. After arriving back to the Jing'an Temple Patrol Room around 1:00PM, they notified the company to retrieve the car.

Suicide Due to Desperation 152

The day before yesterday, a man came to stay at the Dazhong Inn at No. 16 Yangjiadu Street, Wai Ma Road, Nanshi. He registered as Xia Weirong, 22 years old, from Ningbo, and opened room number 11. Unexpectedly, at 11:00 AM yesterday, the tea room saw that he had not yet gotten up and entered the room, discovering that Xia was lying stiff on the bed and was dying. They immediately reported to the accounting room and sent him to the Sixteenth Putili Red Cross Hospital. After being given five injections, he did not recover and died. He was determined to have swallowed a large amount of opium for too long, so he could not be treated. Only five pawn tickets and a letter were found on him. The letter was addressed to Xu Renlin, Dapu Bridge, and mailed from Ningbo. The cause of death was irrelevant. It is thought that he committed suicide because he was desperate. The report was sent to the First District Police Station, and Lu Rongde, the Sixteenth Putili district head, was ordered to report to the local court for an autopsy.

Disaster Area Fire Insurance Compensation Association News 155

The Shanghai Disaster Area Fire Insurance Compensation Association held a plenary committee meeting at its clubhouse on Liu Ma Road at 7:00 PM last night. Chairman Deng Xisheng read out the previous motion, followed by Tang Youwei reporting on the progress in the past week. After discussion, it was generally believed that the foreign merchants had not made any clear statement, so the government bond method was still unable to proceed. At present, the insured in the disaster area were starving, freezing, and had no way to go. Most of the insured held the principle that it was better to die for the public interest of the insured than to starve or freeze to death. The public was extremely agitated and unstoppable. The association should respond to the trend of the insured and quickly determine a method. Therefore, the following cases were agreed upon: ① Publish a warning that all foreign merchants should express their willingness to resign automatically as soon as possible to avoid endangering themselves ② Notify all insured that if foreign insurance companies do not express the same position as Chinese merchants, those who have insured should cancel their insurance and those who have not insured should stop insuring ③ Request the municipal government and the central government to establish insurance businesses in national or local banks and to organize insurance cooperatives by the people ④ Decide to prepare to continue claiming compensation, first ask the executive committee to convene a general meeting quickly to expand the organization ⑤ An extraordinary shareholders meeting must be held every three days to prepare all effective work for practical use ⑥ The executive committee appointed representatives to go to Beijing to petition. The meeting adjourned at 10:00 PM.

Wage Increase Movement for White-Collar Workers Making Small Parts 156

The white-collar workers in the North and South cities who specialize in making barrel parts demanded that the store owners increase their wages by 10 cents per day, starting this month, because their wages were meager and insufficient to make ends meet. The workers petitioned the store owners to increase their wages accordingly. However, the store owners believed that the wage increase was too large, some agreed to increase it by 5 cents, and some prevaricated that it would be implemented uniformly by all stores before they would increase it. The workers were very angry. Yesterday afternoon, they convened a meeting of all workers at the First Spring Restaurant outside the Old North Gate and decided to send representatives to the stores that had not increased wages and the stores that had agreed to increase them by 5 cents to request that they quickly increase wages in consideration of the workers' difficulties. If there were any who refused to increase wages, they would take action. The small parts workers in the Wenzhou-Taizhou gang also demanded a wage increase because their wages were meager. Representatives have now been sent to the union.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Shandong coastal area will be mostly cloudy with southwest winds.
